              Pinterest icon
             </title>

           <a class="fb" data-track="Facebook Share">
            <svg height="36" preserveaspectratio="xMinYMin meet" role="presentation" viewbox="0 0 36 36" width="36" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg">

             </path>

             </path>
            </svg>
           </a>
          </aside>
          <button class="close">
           <svg height="23" preserveaspectratio="xMinYMin meet" viewbox="0 0 23 23" width="23" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg">
            <title>
             Close icon
            </title>
            <path d="M22.6,1.5 L21.8,0.7 C21.4,0.3 20.6,0.3 20.2,0.7 L11.6,9.3 L2.7,0.3 C2.3,-0.1 1.5,-0.1 1.1,0.3 L0.3,1.1 C-0.1,1.5 -0.1,2.3 0.3,2.7 L9.2,11.6 L0.7,20.1 C0.3,20.5 0.3,21.3 0.7,21.7 L1.5,22.5 C1.9,22.9 2.7,22.9 3.1,22.5 L11.6,14 L19.7,22.1 C20.1,22.5 20.9,22.5 21.3,22.1 L22.1,21.3 C22.5,20.9 22.5,20.1 22.1,19.7 L14,11.6 L22.5,3.1 C23,2.7 23,2 22.6,1.5 L22.6,1.5 Z" fill="#000000">
            </path>
           </svg>
          </button>
         </div>
         <figcaption itemprop="caption">
          <cite>
           Photo: Marc Hauser Photography Ltd/Hulton Archive
          </cite>
         </figcaption>
        </figure>
        <p>
         In 2001, author Elmore Leonard,
         <a data-track="Body Text Link: Internal: vulture" href="http://www.vulture.com/2013/08/seitz-on-elmore-leonard-19252013.html">
          who died this morning at the age of 87
         </a>
         , wrote a piece for the New York
         <i>
          Times
         </i>
         in which he laid out, very simply, his ten rules for good writing. You can read the entire piece, with explanations,
         <a data-track="Body Text Link: External" href="http://www.nytimes.com/2001/07/16/arts/writers-writing-easy-adverbs-exclamation-points-especially-hooptedoodle.html">
          over at the
          <i>
           Times
          </i>
          ' site
         </a>
         , but here are the basic precepts. Print them out. Stick them above your desk. Use them wisely.
        </p>
        <ol>
         <li>
          Never open a book with weather.
         </li>
         <li>
          Avoid prologues.
         </li>
         <li>
          Never use a verb other than "said" to carry dialogue.
         </li>
         <li>
          Never use an adverb to modify the verb "said  he admonished gravely.
         </li>
         <li>
          Keep your exclamation points under control. You are allowed no more than two or three per 100,000 words of prose.
         </li>
         <li>
          Never use the words "suddenly" or "all hell broke loose."
         </li>
         <li>
          Use regional dialect, patois, sparingly.
         </li>
         <li>
          Avoid detailed descriptions of characters.
         </li>
         <li>
          Don't go into great detail describing places and things.
         </li>
         <li>
          Try to leave out the part that readers tend to skip.
         </li>
        </ol>
       </div>
       <footer>
       </footer>
      </article>
     </main>
